Pursuant to published notice and public hearing, as required by law, the
Plumbing Code as adopted and amended by the State of Iowa Administrative Code
641 Chapter 25 is hereby adopted by reference as the plumbing code for the City
of Walcott, Iowa, subject to the amendments and adoptions by the State of Iowa.
Fees for permitting shall be as required as adopted in the City of Walcott
Permit Fee Schedule.
(Ord. 534-23 - Jan. 24 Supp.)
160.03   ADOPTION OF IOWA MECHANICAL CODE.  
Pursuant to published notice and public hearing, as required by law, the Iowa
Mechanical Code as adopted and amended by the State of Iowa Administrative Code
641 Chapter 61 is hereby adopted by reference as the mechanical code for the
City of Walcott, Iowa, subject to the amendments and adoptions by the State of
Iowa. Fees for permitting shall be as required as adopted in the City of
Walcott Permit Fee Schedule. The Iowa Mechanical Code, as adopted and amended,
is further amended as follows:
1.   Section 101.1 Title.
   Insert: Walcott, Iowa
(Ord. 534-23 - Jan. 24 Supp.)
160.04   ADOPTION OF NATIONAL ELECTRICAL CODE.
Pursuant to published notice and public hearing, as required by law, the
National Electric Code (NFPA-70) as adopted and amended by the State of Iowa is
hereby adopted by reference as the electrical code for the City of Walcott,
Iowa, subject to the amendments and adoptions by the State of Iowa. Fees for
permitting shall be as required as adopted in the City of Walcott Permit Fee
Schedule. The National Electrical Code as adopted and amended by the State of
Iowa, is further amended as follows:
1.   Minimum size of conductors.
The minimum size of conductors for feeders and branch circuits shall be 12 AWG
and 10 AWG aluminum.
2.   Exposed nonmetallic sheathed cable shall be protected to a height of eight
feet (8') above the floor by approved methods.
(Ord. 534-23 - Jan. 24 Supp.)

prior to issuance of permit. Per Sections 103.22.7 and 105.11.3 of the Code of
Iowa, property owners are not prohibited from performing work on their
principal residence, if it is not larger than a single-family dwelling, or farm

homestead tax exemption.
(Code of Iowa, Sec. 103.22.7 and Sec. 105.11.3)

CHAPTER 161
STORMWATER DETENTION FACILITIES
 
161.01 Purpose                       161.06 Stormwater Detention Plan
                                     Requirements
161.02 Applicability                 161.07 Common Detention Facilities
161.03 Stormwater Detention Criteria 161.08 Completion of Facilities
161.04 Exemptions                    161.09 Responsibilities
161.05 Stormwater Detention Review   161.10 Appeal
 
161.01   PURPOSE.
The purpose of these regulations is to diminish threats to public health,
safety, and welfare caused by increased runoff of stormwater from new
development and redevelopment. This excessive stormwater could result in the
flooding of damageable properties.
161.02   APPLICABILITY.
No building permit shall be issued for the construction, reconstruction, or
structural alteration of a building and/or its parking area, nor shall a
preliminary plat, final plat, or site plan be approved without conformity with
the provisions of this stormwater detention chapter.
161.03   STORMWATER DETENTION CRITERIA.
1.   All stormwater storage areas must be designed to contain and safely pass
stormwater runoff. Adequate spillway provisions shall be provided to transport
peak runoff from a 100-year storm assuming the outlet to be plugged. All
stormwater facilities shall be designed in accordance with the design standards
established by this chapter.
2.   All areas within the City as shown on the map, “Stormwater Detention
Areas,” Figure-1 (on file at City Hall), or any development which, in the
opinion of the City Engineer, lacks an adequate system for the passage of
stormwater, shall comply with this chapter.
   A.   The required stormwater detention shall be that volume necessary to
handle the runoff of a 100-year rainfall, for the critical duration from the
drainage area tributary to the stormwater storage area, less the volume
discharged during the same duration from a five year storm having a runoff
coefficient of “C” = 0.15 when using the Rational Method (for areas of less
than 20 acres) or a curve number of 60 when using the S.C.S. TR-55 Method. The
City may require a lesser release rate when the downstream outlet is
insufficient to safely convey the five-year storm frequency release rate.
   B.   For sites less than 20 acres, the required detention storage (RDS) will
be that found to be the most critical resulting from the inflow from the run-
off of a fully developed tributary area from a 100-year storm and the outflow
of the five-year storm on a predevelopment basis. This can be expressed by the
following equation:
 
      [Inflow rate from]    [Release rate from]   [Duration of the ]
RDS = [critical 100-year] - [ 5-year storm ]    x [critical 100-year]
      [ storm (cfs) ]       [ ]                   [ storm (sec) ]
 
   C.   For sites greater than 20 acres, the method of sizing of the detention
storage volume must be approved by the City Engineer.
3.   Detention storage may be provided as a dry bottom or wet bottom storage
area.
   A.   Dry bottom stormwater storage areas may be designed to serve a
secondary purpose for recreation, open space parking, or other types of uses
that will not be adversely affected by intermittent flooding.
      (1)   (1)   A method of carrying the low flow through these areas shall
be provided in addition to a system of drains to prevent soggy areas.
      (2)   Outlet control structures shall be designed as simply as possible
and shall require little or no attention for proper operation. Each stormwater
storage area shall be provided with a method of emergency overflow in the event
that a storm in excess of the 100-year frequency storm occurs. This emergency
overflow facility shall be designed to function without attention and shall
become part of the excess stormwater passageway. Hydraulic calculations shall
be submitted to the City Engineer to substantiate all design features.
      (3)   Both outlet control structures and emergency overflow facilities
shall be designed and constructed to fully protect the public health, safety,
and welfare. Stormwater runoff velocities shall be kept at a minimum, and
turbulent conditions at an outlet control structure will not be permitted
without complete protection for the public safety. The use of fences shall be
kept to a minimum and used only as a last resort when no other method of
protection is feasible.
      (4)   Paved surfaces that are to serve as stormwater storage shall be
designed with permanent-type control outlets. Emergency overflow areas shall be
provided.
   B.   Wet bottom stormwater storage areas shall be designed with all of the
items required for dry bottom stormwater storage areas, except that the
provisions of Subsection 3(A)(1) of this section shall not be required.
However, the following additional conditions shall be complied with:
      (1)   Water surface areas shall not exceed one-fifteenth of the tributary
drainage area.
      (2)   Facilities shall be provided to lower the pond elevation by gravity
flow for cleaning purposes and shoreline maintenance. Shoreline protection
shall be provided to prevent erosion from wave action.
      (3)   Minimum normal water depth shall be four feet. If fish are to be
maintained, some portion of the pond area should be a minimum of nine feet
deep.
      (4)   Control structures for stormwater release shall be designed to
operate with only a minor increase in the water surface level when the design
storage capacity has been exceeded. Hydraulic calculations shall be submitted
to the City Engineer to substantiate all design features.
161.04   EXEMPTIONS.
The following shall be exempt from these regulations:
1.   Any final plat approved by October 3, 2005, and based upon a preliminary
plat that was approved prior to October 3, 2005, subject to the development not
being required to provide detention facilities by any other ordinances of the
City.
2.   A preliminary or final plat of single-family development consisting of
lots, all of which are one acre or larger.
3.   Any single-family and two-family developed and undeveloped lots which
existed on October 3, 2005.
161.05   STORMWATER DETENTION REVIEW.
1.   For new or expanding commercial, industrial, and multi-family
developments, a stormwater detention plan shall be submitted as part of the
site plan review.
2.   For new single-family and two-family residential developments, a
stormwater detention plan shall be submitted as part of the final plat review.
3.   If no plat or site plan review is required, a stormwater detention plan
must be approved by the City Engineer before a building permit is issued.
161.06   STORMWATER DETENTION PLAN REQUIREMENTS.
Each applicant shall submit all calculations and other such information as
deemed necessary to demonstrate to the City Engineer the stormwater runoff rate
and capacity of stormwater storage facilities. Required information may vary
according to the size of development, and shall include, but not be limited to,
the following:
1.   Map of the property and immediate vicinity showing elevation of contours.
2.   Mapping and description of existing and proposed drainage system features
of the property and immediate vicinity.
3.   Physical features of the property and immediate vicinity including, but
not limited to, the state and type of development in the area, public
infrastructure, and other similar characteristics.
161.07   COMMON DETENTION FACILITIES.
The City may, in lieu of on-site detention facilities, accept off-site
detention facilities. Until such time as the permanent off-site stormwater
detention facilities are available, temporary on-site detention shall be
provided. An acceptable legal contract between the developer and the off-site
land owner shall be approved by the City Council.
161.08   COMPLETION OF FACILITIES.
The stormwater detention facilities shall be constructed and in use in
accordance with the following criteria.
1.   For commercial, industrial, and multi-family developments, the facilities
shall be constructed concurrent with site grading. A certificate of completion
shall be furnished by the developer’s Engineer certifying that they have been
constructed according to the approved plans before a certificate of occupancy
is issued by the City.
2.   For single-family and two-family residential building, the developer’s
Engineer shall certify that the public improvements have been substantially
complete, and the detention facility rough graded, before a building permit is
issued. A certificate of completion shall be furnished by the Engineer
certifying that the facilities into which the lots drain have been constructed
according to the approved plans before a certificate of occupancy permit is
issued by the City.
161.09   RESPONSIBILITIES.
Industrial, commercial, condominium, and multi-family developments, and single-
family or two-family lots or development with individual detention facilities
shall meet the following requirements:
1.   The developer shall be responsible for providing a plan of ownership of
the detention facilities involving a single owner, an association, or another
plan of ownership approved by the City.
2.   The owner shall be responsible to insure the continuing functioning of the
facility as originally designed and intended. All plans submitted for
stormwater detention systems shall describe an adequate procedure for normal
maintenance for the detention system. Any failure of the stormwater detention
system due to inadequate normal or capital maintenance shall be the
responsibility of the owner of the property on which the detention system is
located. It shall also be the property owner’s responsibility to remedy any
negligence in maintenance that resulted in the failure of the system. The
submittal of plans for such a system or the purchase of property on which such
system is located shall be deemed as acceptance of responsibility for normal
and capital maintenance of system.
3.   The developer shall dedicate an easement to the City reserving the land
for use as a stormwater detention facility providing the City with the right to
inspect the facility, and the necessary easements for ingress and egress.
4.   The City shall provide inspection of the detention facilities as deemed
appropriate. If any maintenance work is necessary, the City shall serve a
written order to the owner of the facilities, specifying therein the work
necessary to be done and providing for a reasonable time for its completion.
Any property owner to whom an order is directed shall have the right to appeal
to the City Council. Unless the order is revoked or modified, it shall remain
in full force and be obeyed by the owner as directed within the time
established by the City. When an owner to whom an order has been issued fails
to comply within the time specified, the City shall remedy the condition, or
contract with others for such purpose, and charge all costs, including
administration, to whom the order is directed. If the cost of remedying a
condition is not paid within 30 days after the mailing of a statement from the
City, the cost shall be assessed against the property for collection in the
same manner as a property tax. In the event the association fails or is unable
to pay the costs associated with detention facility maintenance, these costs
shall be assessed against those users of the facility based upon their
percentage of use. The provisions of this subparagraph shall be applicable to
any stormwater detention facility in existence as of the effective date
of Ordinance No. 415-05 codified by this chapter, notwithstanding any
provisions of Paragraph D above or any other provisions limiting the
applicability of the provisions of this chapter.
161.10   APPEAL.
The City Council may, in the resolution approving the preliminary plat of any
subdivision, and, upon appeal of the developer or the recommendation of the
City Engineer, waive or change the requirements of this chapter for a
particular development whenever the developer demonstrates either:
1.   That, due to the location of the property, strict compliance would provide
no discernible benefit for reduction of flooding on any adjacent or downstream
property; or
2.   That, due to the nature of the property, strict compliance would create
unusual hardship out of proportion to any foreseeable benefit, and that the
requested change or reduction in requirements will not increase the risk of
flooding of any building or the buildable portion of any lot on any adjacent or
downstream property.
CHAPTER 162
RENTAL HOUSING CODE
 
162.01 Title                            162.06 Inspections
162.02 Purpose                          162.07 Rental Housing Code Fee Schedule
162.03 Administration and Enforcement   162.08 Notice of Violations
162.04 Scope                            162.09 Appeals
162.05 Requirements for Rental Property 162.10 Conflict of Ordinances
 
162.01   TITLE.
These regulations shall be known as the Rental Housing Code, and may be cited
as such and will be referred to herein as “this code”.
162.02   PURPOSE.
1.   The purpose of this code is to provide minimum standards to safeguard life
or limb, health, property, and public welfare by regulating and controlling the
use and occupancy, location, and maintenance of all residential dwellings and
structures which are rental occupied within this jurisdiction.
2.   The purpose of this code is not to create or otherwise establish or
designate any particular class or group of persons who will, or should be,
especially protected or benefited by the terms of this code.
162.03   ADMINISTRATION AND ENFORCEMENT.
1.   Administration and enforcement is a function of the Building Department of
the City.
2.   This code has been adopted and is to be used in conjunction with other
City codes, including codes as amended and adopted in
Chapter 160, including, but not limited to, requirements of the International
Property Maintenance Code, and should not be construed to include all
regulations pertaining to buildings and development. Nothing in this chapter
shall be interpreted as prohibiting or limiting enforcement by the Building
Inspector or any other department of the City, County, or State codes and
ordinances as adopted and amended by those respective jurisdictions.
162.04   SCOPE.
The provisions of this code apply to all residential rental properties or
portions thereof used or designed, or intended to be used, for human
habitation, whether vacant or occupied. This code shall further apply to all
accessory structures and any nuisance as defined by this Code of Ordinances or
codes adopted by the City that may exist in a building or the building’s yard.
162.05   REQUIREMENTS FOR RENTAL PROPERTY.
1.   General. It shall be a violation of this code for any person to let to
another for rent and/or occupancy, except in compliance with the provisions of
the City's Rental Housing Guide, any dwelling, dwelling unit, duplex, multi-
family dwelling, sleeping room, single-family dwelling, or condominium unless
the owner or agent holds a valid Certificate of Structural Compliance/Rental
License, issued by the City, applicable to those portions of the specific
structure used for residential rental purposes or affecting any areas used for
residential rental purposes.
(Ord. 533-23 - Jan. 24 Supp.)
2.   Certificate of Structural Compliance/Rental License (referred to as
Certificate). The Certificate, when issued, shall certify that the requirements
of this code are met. The Certificate shall be transferable at the time of a
change in ownership and shall be maintained as a public record of the City. The
owner or agent shall notify the City of any change of interest or ownership in
the property within 30 days of any conveyance or transfer of interest affecting
the property, and provide the name and address of all persons who have acquired
an interest therein. The Certificate shall state the date of issuance and the
address of the structure to which it is applicable. All dwelling units and
sleeping rooms being let for rent and/or occupancy without a valid Certificate
may be ordered vacated.
3.   Issuance of Certificate. When the provisions of this code have been
complied with by the owner or operator, along with payment of the required fees
(fees shall be set by resolution of the City Council), the City shall issue a
Certificate. The Certificate will remain valid until the property’s next
required inspection.
4.   Revocation of Certificate. When there exists a material and substantial
noncompliance with this code which directly affects the health, life, safety,
or property of the occupants or the public, the City may revoke the Certificate
in whole, or modify the Certificate to reflect the compliance of each separate
dwelling unit or sleeping room within a structure. The owner or agent of the
affected property shall be notified in writing by certified mail of the license
revocation.
162.06   INSPECTIONS.
1.   Dwelling Inspection Schedule. Rental properties in substantial compliance
will be placed on a two-year inspection schedule. All other rental properties
will be inspected annually. Compliance determination will be the responsibility
of the Building Inspector.
2.   Appointments for Inspections. Appointment for inspections for the owner/
agent of the building shall be scheduled by the Building Inspector. The owner/
agent may request the appointment to be rescheduled. However, the inspection
shall be performed within 30 days of the original date. An owner/agent shall be
required to arrange for access to all portions of the building. Failure to
provide access to all portions of the building shall prevent the issuance of a
Certificate, and thus compliance with the law. The owner/agent shall notify all
tenants of the inspection in accordance with the Chapter 562A of the Code of
Iowa, Uniform Residential Landlord and Tenant Law.
3.   General Procedures for Inspections. Inspections shall not be:
   A.   Conducted with a minor as the sole representative of the owner.
   B.   Conducted against the will of the tenant without the building owner/
agent present.
   C.   Conducted without prior notice to the tenant, as required by State law.
   D.   Conducted of an occupied dwelling without the owner/agent or tenant of
the dwelling or designated agent being present.
4.   Admittance to Unit. Should the person in control of the unit refuse
admittance to the Building Inspector or designee, and refuse to reschedule the
licensing inspection or re-inspection, the Building Inspector may request that
a court of competent jurisdiction issue an administrative search warrant.
5.   Inspection. All areas of each dwelling governed by this chapter shall be
inspected. Should access not be obtained to all areas, a re-inspection must be
scheduled and an additional fee may be charged for each subsequent re-
inspection in accordance with the established fee schedule.
162.07   RENTAL HOUSING CODE FEE SCHEDULE.
Fees shall be charged for services rendered in relation to this chapter. These
services include, but are not limited to, the following: certification,
licenses, re-inspections, failure to appear for inspections or re-inspections,
late cancellations, and appeals. Fees will be assessed on a two-year schedule
for those properties in substantial compliance, and annually for those
properties on an annual inspection schedule. The amount shall be established by
resolution of the City Council.
162.08   NOTICE OF VIOLATIONS.
Whenever the appropriate authority determines that any rented residential
structure, or the premises surrounding any of these, fails to meet the
requirements set forth in this code or in applicable rules and regulations
issued pursuant thereto, a notice shall be issued setting forth the alleged
failures and advising the owner, occupant, or agent that such failures must be
corrected. This notice shall:
1.   Be in writing.
2.   Set forth the alleged violations of this code and applicable rules and
regulations issued pursuant thereto.
3.   Describe the residential structure where the violations are alleged to
exist or to have been committed.
4.   Provide a reasonable time, not to exceed 60 days, for correction of non-
substantial violations, or not to exceed 10 days for substantial violations.
This provision shall not prohibit revocation of the Certificate as may be
necessary.
5.   Be served upon the owner or legal agent of the residential structure by
certified mail addressed to the same at the most current address maintained in
the records of the County Assessor.
6.   At the end of the time period allowed for the correction of violations,
the property shall be re-inspected for compliance. Upon failure to correct
violations, a criminal or municipal citation will be issued.
162.09   APPEALS.
1.   General.  Any person aggrieved by any order, requirement, decision, or
determination made by the Building Inspector on all matters pertaining to
buildings, structures, or occupancy included in this chapter has the right to
appeal to the City Council. An appeal may be submitted to the City Council
within 10 working days of the Building Inspector’s decision, and, upon payment
of a fee, established by Council resolution, to the City. The appeal must
include the reason for the appeal and a statement detailing relief requested.
2.   Following the receipt of an appeal request, the City Council will hold a
hearing within 30 days at which time the petitioner shall be given an
opportunity to show just cause why the notice or order should be modified or
withdrawn, or why the period of time permitted for compliance should be
extended.
3.   The City Council shall have the power to affirm, modify, or revoke the
notice or order, grant variances from the provisions of this code or from
applicable rules and regulations issued pursuant thereto, or to grant an
extension of time for the performance of any act required where the City
Council finds there is practical difficulty or undue hardship connected with
the performance of any act required by the provisions of this code or by
applicable rules or regulations issued pursuant thereto and that such extension
is in harmony with the general purpose of this code to secure the public
health, safety, and welfare.
162.10   CONFLICT OF ORDINANCES.
In any case where a provision of this code is found to be in conflict with a
provision of any zoning, building, fire, safety, or health ordinance or Code of
the City existing on the effective date hereof, the provision which establishes
the higher standard for the practical promotion and protection of the health
and safety of the people shall prevail. In any case, where a provision of this
Code is found to be in conflict with a provision of any other ordinance or Code
of the City existing on the effective date hereof which establishes a lower
standard for the promotion and protection of the health and safety of the
people, the provisions of this Code shall be deemed to prevail, and such other
ordinances or Codes are hereby declared to be repealed to the extent that they
may be found in conflict with this Code.
CHAPTER 165
SIGNS
 
165.01 Purpose and Intent              165.05 Permitted Signs in All Zones
165.02 Definitions                     165.06 Signs Permitted by Zone
165.03 Permit Required                 165.07 Prohibited Signs
165.04 General Rules and Applicability
 
165.01   PURPOSE AND INTENT.
These sign regulations are intended to enhance and protect the physical
appearance and safety of the community, and to protect property values. These
regulations are also intended to reduce distractions and obstructions
contributing to traffic accidents, reduce hazards caused by signs projecting
over public right-of-way, provide a reasonable opportunity for all sign users
to display signs without interference from other signage, to provide fair and
equitable treatment for all sign users, and to establish a reasonable period of
time for elimination of nonconforming signs.
165.02   DEFINITIONS.
For use in this chapter, the following definitions are given:
1.   “Advertising sign” means a sign displaying the type or name of a product,
good, or service sold either on or off premises on which the sign is located.
2.   “Animated sign” means any sign or part of a sign that moves.
3.   “Awning sign” means a building sign placed on the surface of an awning.
4.   “Banner” means a strip of flexible material, such as cloth, paper, or
plastic, securely fastened on all corners to a building or structure and used
to advertise a special event.
5.   “Billboard” means an off-premises sign on which poster panels or bulletins
are mounted. Billboard signs are not freestanding signs or monument signs.
6.   “Building sign” means any sign attached to a building or to an
appurtenance of a building in any way.
7.   “Canopy sign” means a building sign attached to, or in any way
incorporated with, the face or underside of a canopy, marquee, or any other
similar building projection and which does not extend beyond the projection by
more than six inches.
8.   “Changeable copy sign” means a sign, such as a reader board, with
components easily changeable by physical and not electronic methods.
9.   “Common sign” means a sign which serves two or more uses.
10.   “Construction sign” means a sign identifying the architects, engineers,
contractors, and other individuals involved in the construction of a building,
or announcing the future use of the building.
11.   “Development sign” means a sign designating the name of a development or
subdivision consisting of two or more acres.
12.   “Directional arrow sign” means a sign used to direct people and vehicular
traffic.
13.   “Directional sign” means a sign designed to guide or direct pedestrian or
vehicular traffic and containing no advertising message.
14.   “Directory sign” means a sign displaying the name of a building, building
complex, and/or the occupants.
15.   “Drive-through restaurant menu sign” means a sign displaying a menu or
similar advertising for the purpose of allowing patrons of a restaurant to
order food at a drive-through facility.
16.   “Electronic sign” means a sign which displays a changing message through
the use of an electronically controlled and illuminated medium. An electronic
sign is not considered an animated sign.
17.   “Fascia sign” means a single-faced building sign parallel to or at an
angle of not more than 45 degrees from the wall of the building on which it is
mounted. Such signs do not extend more than one foot out from vertical walls or
more than one foot out at the sign’s closest point from non-vertical walls.
18.   “Filling stations signs” means signage which generally appears as a
integral part of the equipment accessory to automotive service stations and
other establishments engaged in the dispensing of motor vehicle fuel or oil,
including, but not limited to, gasoline pumps, oil display racks, and portable
tire racks.
19.   “Flag, private” means any flag displaying the name, insignia, logo, or
emblem of an individual or a profit-making entity.
20.   “Flag, public” means any flag displaying the name, insignia, logo of the
United States, the State of Iowa, the City, or a nonprofit organization or
institution.
21.   “Freestanding sign” means a sign supported by one or more uprights or
braces firmly and permanently anchored in or on the ground and not attached to
any building or wall.
22.   “Going out of business sign” means a sign announcing a sale resulting
from the termination of a business on the premises.
23.   “Grand opening sign” – See “special events sign.”
24.   “Hazardous sign” means a sign which, because of its construction or state
of disrepair, may fall or cause possible injury to passerby, as determined by
the City; or a sign which, because of its location, color, illumination, or
animation, interferes with, obstructs the view of, or is confused with any
authorized traffic sign or device; or a sign which makes use of the words
“stop,” “go slow,” “caution,” “danger,” or any other word, phrase, symbol, or
character in such a way as to interfere with, mislead or confuse traffic.
25.   “Identification sign” means a sign displaying the name, address, crest,
insignia, trademark, occupation, or profession of an occupant of a building or
the name of any building on the premises.
26.   “Illuminated sign” means any sign in which a source of light is used to
make the message readable. An illuminated sign need not be an electronic sign.
27.   “Institutional sign” means a sign which displays the name of a religious
institution, school, library, community center, civic, cultural or historic
institutions, nursing home, hospital, or similar institution, and announces its
services or activities.
28.   “Integral sign” means a sign carved into stone, concrete or other
building material or made of bronze, aluminum, or other permanent type of
construction and made a part of the building to which it is attached.
29.   “Marquee sign” – See “canopy sign.”
30.   “Monument sign” means a sign displaying the name, address, crest,
insignia, trademark, occupation, or profession of occupants of the building, or
the name of the building, and firmly anchored to the ground. Such a sign does
not contain any advertising or promotional information.
31.   “Nonconforming sign” means a sign, other than a prohibited sign, that
does not comply with the regulations of the zone in which it is located by
reason of these or any other regulations adopted after the installation of the
sign.
32.   “Obsolete sign” means a sign that advertises an activity, business, or a
service no longer conducted.
33.   “Off-premises sign” means a sign which directs attention to a use
conducted off the lot on which the sign is located.
34.   “On-premises sign” means a sign with the primary purpose of identifying
or directing attention to the lot on which the sign is located.
35.   “Painted sign” means a sign painted directly on an exterior surface of a
building other than on the windows.
36.   “Parapet sign” means a fascia sign installed on a parapet or a parapet
wall.
37.   “Permitted sign” means a sign allowed in the zone in which it is listed,
subject to compliance with the requirements of the sign regulations.
38.   “Political sign” means a temporary sign announcing candidates seeking
public office, a political issue, or containing other election information,
such as “vote today,” are not considered off-premises signs.
39.   “Portable sign” means a sign not firmly and permanently anchored or
secured to either a building or the ground and not expressly permitted under
these regulations as a temporary sign.
40.   “Poster” means a temporary sign on a card or sheet of paper, plastic, or
similar material intended to advertise or publicize a product or event.
41.   “Prohibited sign” means a sign, other than a nonconforming sign, not
permitted by this chapter.
42.   “Projecting sign” means a building sign extending more than one foot out
from the wall of the building on which it is mounted.
43.   “Provisional sign” means a sign permitted in a zone under certain
circumstances.
44.   “Public art” means any work of art exposed to public view from any street
right-of-way which does not contain any advertising, commercial symbolism (such
as logos and trademarks), or any representation of a product.
45.   “Public sign” means a noncommercial sign installed by or on the order of
authorization of the City or other public agency in the public interest. Such
signs include, but are not limited to, safety signs, zoning signs, memorial
plaques, signs for structures or sites of historical interest, and all similar
signs.
46.   “Real estate sign” means a sign which advertises the sale, rental, or
lease of the premises, or part of the premises, including open house and parade
of homes directional signs.
47.   “Roof sign” means a sign installed on or above a roof of a building and
affixed to the roof.
48.   “Seasonal decoration” means a display, which does not constitute a sign,
pertaining to recognized national, State, or local holidays and observances.
49.   “Sign” means any structure or medium, including its component parts,
visible to the public from a street or public right-of-way and used or intended
to be used to direct attention to a business, product, service, subject, idea,
premises, or thing. “Sign” does not include buildings or landscaping. The term
“sign” includes, but is not limited to, all reading matter, letters, numerals,
pictorial representation, emblems, trademarks, inscriptions, and patterns,
whether affixed to a building or separate from a building. This definition does
not include public area, seasonal decorations, and directional symbols on paved
surfaces.
50.   “Sign face” means the surface of the sign on which reading material,
letters, numerals, pictorial representations, emblems, trademarks,
inscriptions, and/or patterns are affixed.
51.   “Special events sign” means a sign announcing grand openings,
philanthropic events, events of nonprofit organizations, or events of civic
interest.
52.   “Spinner” means a device shaped like a propeller and designed to rotate
in the wind to attract attention to the premises on which it is located.
53.   “Swinging sign” means a sign which, because of its design, construction,
suspension, or attachment, is free to swing or move noticeably because of
pressure from the wind.
54.   “Temporary sign” means a sign constructed of temporary materials, such as
cardboard, wallboard, or plywood, with or without a structural frame, intended
for a temporary period of display, such as yard sale signs, temporary
identification signs, and political signs, but excluding banners.
55.   “Time and temperature sign” means an identification sign which shows the
current time and temperature in an electronic digital format. At least 40
percent of each sign face shall be devoted to the display of time and
temperature.
56.   “Use” means a “principal use” as defined in this chapter.
57.   “Wall sign” means a sign on the wall of a building on which a sign is
mounted, including elements of the wall or any member or group of members which
defines the exterior boundaries of the side of the building on which the sign
is mounted and which has a slope of 45 degrees or greater with the horizontal
plane.
58.   “Window sign” means a building sign permanently affixed to a window,
embedded in a window, or hanging adjacent to a window, and obviously intended
to be viewed by the public through the window. This definition does not include
merchandise or product displays, posters, signs painted on windows, and
temporary signs.
59.   “Yard sale sign” means a temporary sign advertising a yard sale or garage
sale.
165.03   PERMIT REQUIRED.
No sign requiring a permit shall be installed, erected, moved, altered,
improved, or converted without obtaining a sign permit from the Building
Official and making payment of the required permit fee (unless specifically
exempted by provisions of this chapter). Each sign requires a separate sign
permit. Every applicant before being issued a sign permit shall pay to the City
such fee as shall be established by resolution of the Council based on Uniform
Building Code fees the City has adopted.
165.04   GENERAL RULES AND APPLICABILITY.
1.   Compliance Required. No sign on private property shall be installed or
changed in any manner without compliance with the regulations stated herein.
   A.   No signs are permitted in the City right-of-way or on City property
unless specifically approved by the Council.
   B.   Routine maintenance is not subject to this chapter.
2.   Prohibited Signs. These regulations are intended to be exclusionary. Any
sign not specifically listed shall be prohibited.
3.   Categories of Signs. These regulations are broken down into two general
categories of temporary and permanent signs.
   A.   Temporary Signs. Temporary signs are governed by the provisions of
subsection 165.05(1)(H).
   B.   Permanent Signs. Permanent signs may be either off-premises or on-
premises signs. Off-premises signs are governed by the provisions of subsection
165.05(2)(J). All on-premises signs are governed by the regulations of the zone
in which they are located.
4.   Size.
   A.   In all zones, a maximum sign allowance is permitted for all permanent
signs placed on a building. Any quantity or type of building sign may be
installed within this maximum allowance and according to the specific
requirements of the zone in which the building is located.
   B.   The building sign allowance shall relate to the wall on which a sign is
to be placed and shall be determined by calculating a percentage of the total
square footage of the sign wall, as specified in the zone. In the case of two
or more uses or occupants in a single building, the total building signage on a
wall for all the uses shall not exceed the maximum building sign allowance for
that wall.
   C.   Freestanding signs, monument signs, or any other signs not mounted on a
building are not included in this maximum building sign allowance and are
governed by the specific requirements of the zone.
5.   Application of State Law. In any case in which the Code of Iowa, as
amended, contains more restrictive requirements than the regulations contained
herein, the Code of Iowa, as amended, shall apply.
165.05   PERMITTED SIGNS IN ALL ZONES.
1.   Signs Not Requiring a Permit. The following signs may be installed in
addition to the signage permitted in each zone without obtaining a permit.
These signs shall not be applied towards the maximum sign allowance specified
in the zones, except as otherwise indicated in this section.
   A.   Non-illuminated construction signs not to exceed a total of 64 square
feet or 32 square feet per sign face shall be permitted for each lot. Such
signs shall not exceed a height of five feet in residential zones or 10 feet in
other zones. The sign shall not be located closer than five feet to any
property line unless located on the wall of a building, fence, or protective
barricade surrounding the construction. Construction signs shall be removed
prior to the issuance of the certificate of occupancy.
   B.   Filling station signs.
   C.   Identification signs not exceeding two square feet in area.
   D.   Informational window signs displaying information about the operation
of the business, including, but not limited to, days and hours of operation,
telephone number, and credit cards or bank cards accepted. Such signs shall not
exceed a maximum area of two square feet.
   E.   One private flag displayed in conjunction with public flag.
   F.   Public signs.
   G.   One non-illuminated real estate sign, not to exceed a total of four
square feet or two square feet per sign face in residential zones, or a total
of 64 square feet or 32 square feet per sign face in other zones. Such signs
shall not exceed a height of five feet in residential zones, or 10 feet in
other zones, or be closer than two feet to any property line unless located on
the wall of a building. Such signs shall be removed within 48 hours after the
closing of the property. These signs are required to be 30 feet back from an
intersection.
   H.   Temporary signs are prohibited except for real estate signs, garage
sale signs, Happy Birthday signs, and other like signs. Temporary signs may be
displayed, but shall not be illuminated more than three square feet in area,
and shall not be displayed for a period exceeding 10 days.
   I.   Posters and other non-permanent signs in windows.
2.   Signs Requiring a Permit. The following signs may be installed in
accordance with the dimensional requirements of the zone in which the sign is
located.
   A.   Changeable copy signs shall be installed in accordance with the
dimensional requirements of the zone in which the sign is located.
   B.   Development signs, including one monument sign in P.U.D. and R Zones
and one monument or freestanding sign in other zones, shall be permitted at
each street entrance to a subdivision, provided the following requirements are
met.
      (1)   In S.A. and R Zones, the sign shall not exceed a total area of 64
square feet or 32 square feet per sign face, and shall not exceed a height of
five feet, and shall be no closer than 30 feet from an intersection.
      (2)   In other zones, the sign shall not exceed the size and height
limitations for the same type of sign, i.e., freestanding or monument sign,
permitted in the zone and for the lot on which the sign is located.
   C.   Directional signs shall not exceed a total of four square feet per sign
face in R Zones, or a total of eight square feet per sign face in all other
zones, and with a five-foot required setback from the property line. For
directional arrow signs, the maximum size is eight inches high, 24 inches long
on a single post. This sign may be placed within an intersection but not on
public land or street right-of-way unless expressly approved by the Council.
   D.   Directory sign.
   E.   Drive-through restaurant menu signs may not exceed 150 square feet in
total square footage. These signs shall be in addition to the signs permitted
in the zone and shall not be applied toward the maximum sign allowance.
   F.   Going out of business signs shall be non-illuminated and shall not
exceed 100 square feet. A going-out-of-business sign may be displayed for up to
60 days. The sign permit shall be automatically renewed with the renewal of a
going-out-of-business license so long as the total time period in which the
sign is displayed does not exceed 90 days. The use of going-out-of-business
signs is restricted to one time in a 12-month period for a single business.
Going-out-of-business signs shall not be applied towards the maximum signage
allowance specified in each zone.
   G.   One institutional sign, not to exceed a total of 48 square feet or 24
square feet per sign face, shall be permitted for each institution. No such
sign shall exceed a height of five feet above grade.
   H.   Integral signs existing prior to the effective date hereof shall not be
applied toward the maximum sign allowance of the building to which they are
attached.
   I.   Real estate development signs, consisting of one non-illuminated
monument real estate sign not to exceed a total of 64 square feet or 32 square
feet per sign face, shall be permitted per subdivision or development of
greater than two acres in size. Such signs shall not exceed a height of 10 feet
and shall be removed upon the sale or lease of 75 percent of the lots or units
in the subdivision or development. These signs shall not be applied toward the
maximum signage allowance specified in each zone. Large-scale real estate signs
shall not be considered off-premises signs.
   J.   Off-premises signs:
      (1)   Off-premises signs shall not be permitted in residential zones. In
the commercial zones, only off-premises fascia signs shall be allowed. Off-
premises signs may be billboard signs or any other type of sign allowed in the
zone in which the sign is located.
      (2)   Not more than one off-premises sign may be installed or maintained
per lot or parcel of land. Two or more businesses may install a common off-
premises directional sign. No off-premises sign shall be located closer than
300 feet to another off-premises sign.
      (3)   No off-premises sign shall be located within 120 feet of a
residential zone, a public park, parochial school, religious institution,
cemetery, public museum, or the administrative or judicial offices of City,
County, State, or federal government.
      (4)   An off-premises sign shall be permitted in addition to the on-
premises signage. The off-premises sign shall not be deducted from the total
sign area allowed for the same type of on-premises signage.
      (5)   (Repealed by Ord. 541-23 - Jan. 24 Supp.)
      (6)   (Repealed by Ord. 541-23 - Jan. 24 Supp.)
      (7)   Off-premises signs shall comply with all other sign requirements of
the zone in which they are located.
   K.   A special events sign, consisting of one non-illuminated sign not to
exceed 100 square feet, is permitted on a lot. The use of a special events sign
is restricted to no more than four times in a 12-month period and for a single
duration of no more than 30 days. Special events signs may include banners, but
shall not include any sign prohibited by Section
165.07 of this chapter. Special events signs shall not be applied toward the
maximum signage allowance specified in each zone.
   L.   (Repealed by Ord. 541-23 - Jan. 24 Supp.)  
165.06   SIGNS PERMITTED BY ZONE.
1.   S.A., R., and P.U.D. Zones.
   A.   Permitted Signs.
      (1)   Principal uses other than single-family dwellings and duplexes
shall be permitted one identification fascia, awning, or monument sign.
      (2)   Nonresidential uses in the S.A. zone, other than uses permitted,
shall be required to comply with the sign regulations of the C-1 and C-2 zones.
      (3)   Residential uses in the P.U.D. zone shall be permitted signage in
accordance with the requirements of the R zone.
      (4)   Signs in City-owned parks located in R-1 Districts shall be in
accordance with the sign regulations of the C-1 and C-2 Zones.
   B.   Dimensional Requirements.
      (1)   Awning Signs in S.A., R-1, R-2, R-4 Zones:
Maximum Area – 25 percent of the surface of the awning or 12 square feet,
whichever is less
Maximum Height – top of first story
      (2)   Monument Signs in S.A., R-1, R-2, R-4 Zones:
Maximum Area – 24 square feet, or 12 square feet per sign face
Maximum Height – five feet
      (3)   Monument Signs in R-3 Zones:
Maximum Area – 24 square feet or 12 square feet per sign face
Maximum Height – five feet
      (4)   Wall and Fascia Signs in S.A., R-1, R-2, R-4:
Maximum Area – four square feet
Maximum Height – top of first story
      (5)   Wall and Fascia Signs in R-3 Zones:
Maximum Area – 12 square feet
Maximum Height – top of first story
2.   Neighborhood Local Business (C-1).
   A.   Permitted Signs.
      (1)   Signage for existing residential uses shall comply with the
requirements for residential uses in R zones.
      (2)   Awning signs.
      (3)   Canopy signs.
      (4)   Electronic signs.
      (5)   Fascia signs.
      (6)   Freestanding signs.
      (7)   Monument signs.
      (8)   Wall signs.
      (9)   Window signs.
   B.   Provisional Signs.
      (1)   When two or more uses are located on a lot, a common monument sign
shall be permitted. Said sign shall not exceed the lesser of two square feet
per lineal foot of lot frontage, or 100 square feet, or 50 square feet per sign
face.
      (2)   Barber pole signs, provided they do not exceed three feet in length
and nine inches in diameter.
      (3)   Time and temperature signs which do not exceed 100 square feet in
area or 50 square feet per sign face and are not less than 10 feet above grade.
   C.   Dimensional Requirements.
      (1)   Maximum Building Sign Area. Uses in these zones shall be allowed a
maximum building sign area per sign wall equal to 15 percent of the sign wall
on which the sign is to be mounted.
      (2)   Individual Sign Allowances.
Awning Signs:       maximum area: none
                    maximum height: top of first story

                    maximum height: top of first story
                    maximum area: 100 square feet or 50 square feet per sign

                    maximum height: none

      (2)   Awning signs.

      (2)   Barber pole signs, provided they do not exceed three feet in length
and nine inches in diameter.
      (3)   When two or more uses are located on a lot, a common monument sign
may be installed.
      (4)   When two or more uses are located on a lot, a common monument or
freestanding sign may be installed. The maximum area of the common sign may be
50 percent larger than the area of the maximum individual sign allowed.

4.   Interstate Highway Commercial District (C-3).
   A.   Permitted Signs.
      (1)   Signage for existing residential uses shall comply with sign
requirements for residential uses in the R-3 zone.
      (2)   Awning signs.
      (3)   Billboard Signs
      (4)   Canopy signs.
      (5)   Electronic signs.
      (6)   Entrance and exit signs (maximum eight square feet per face).
      (7)   Fascia signs.
      (8)   Freestanding signs.
      (9)   Monument signs.
      (10)   Wall signs.
      (11)   Window signs.
(Ord. 541-23 - Jan. 24 Supp.)
   B.   Provisional Signs.
      (1)   When two or more uses are located on a lot, a common monument or
freestanding sign may be installed. The maximum area of the common sign may be
50 percent larger than the area of the maximum individual sign allowed.
      (2)   Two freestanding signs and one monument sign are permitted per
address, provided frontage along a single lot is not less than 160 feet. The
distance between two freestanding signs shall be no less than 150 feet as
measured along the frontage of a single lot. For interior lots, the distance
between two freestanding signs shall be no less than 150 feet.
      (3)   Time and temperature signs which do not exceed 100 square feet in
area or 50 square feet per sign face and are not less than 10 feet above grade.
   C.   Dimensional Requirements.
      (1)   Individual Signage Allowances.
Awning Signs:           maximum area: none
                        maximum height: top of first story
                        maximum area: 672 square feet per sign face.
Billboard Signs:        maximum height: 107 feet above the crown of the
                        overpass on I-80 and Y-40 roads

                        maximum area: two square feet per lineal foot of lot

                        maximum height: 20 feet
Wall Signs:             maximum area: 50 percent of the sign wall
                        maximum height: none
Window Signs:           maximum area: none
                        maximum height: none
 
      (3)   Design Criteria Required. All signs constructed in the C-3 Zone
District shall be required to comply with a 90 MPH wind load for the structure
and sign frame assembly. Design and plans shall be stamped by an Iowa
Registered Engineer.
5.   M Zones.
   A.   Permitted Signs.
      (1)   Awning signs.
      (2)   Electronic signs.
      (3)   Fascia signs.
      (4)   Identification freestanding signs.
      (5)   Identification monument signs.
      (6)   Wall signs.
      (7)   Window signs.
   B.   Provisional Signs.
      (1)   When two or more uses are located on a lot, a common mounted or
freestanding sign may be installed. The maximum area of the common sign may be
50 percent larger than the area of the maximum individual sign allowance.
      (2)   In M Zones, two freestanding or monument signs may be permitted,
provided frontage along a single lot is not less than 160 feet. The distance
between the two signs shall be not less than 150 feet measured along the
frontage.
   C.   Dimensional Requirements:
      (1)   Maximum Building Sign Area. Uses in this zone shall be allowed a
maximum building sign area per sign wall equal to 50 percent of the sign wall
on which the sign is to be located.
      (2)   Individual Signage Allowances.

Freestanding Signs: exceed 100 square feet or 50 square feet per sign face

                    maximum height: 10 feet
Wall Signs:         maximum area: 25 percent of the sign wall
                    maximum height: top of first story
Window Signs:       maximum area: none;
                    maximum height: none
 
165.07   PROHIBITED SIGNS.
The following signs are specifically prohibited in all zones:
1.   Animated signs, excluding barber pole signs that do not exceed three feet
in height and nine inches in diameter, and excluding time and temperature
signs, and excluding changing message signs.
2.   Hazardous signs.
3.   Obsolete signs.
4.   Portable signs, including signs on wheels and excluding those temporary
signs expressly permitted herein.
5.   Roof signs, unless complying with the City Building Code.
6.   Search lights.
7.   Spinners or other similar devices.
8.   Swinging signs.
9.   Signs not anchored for wind load except real estate or like signs.

166.01   ESTABLISHMENT OF CONTROL.
No land shall be subdivided or filed for record, nor any street laid out, nor
any improvements made to the land, until the plat or plans of the subdivision
or street improvements shall have been referred to the Planning and Zoning
Commission for review and recommendation and approved by action of the Council.
This approval must be in writing and place the original tracing of the final
plat according to the procedure outlined in this chapter. No lot, tract, or
parcel of land within any such subdivision shall be offered for sale, nor shall
any sale, contract for sale, or option be made or given, until such subdivision
plans have been properly reviewed by the Planning and Zoning Commission and
officially approved by the Council. No improvements, such as sidewalks, water
supply, stormwater drainage, sewer facilities, gas service, electric service,
or lighting, or grading, paving, or surfacing of streets, shall be made within
any such subdivision by any owner or owner’s agent, or by any public service
corporation at the request of such owner or agent, until a preliminary plat for
the subdivision and also the plans for improvements thereto have been formally
approved by Planning and Zoning Commission and Council. The restrictions set
forth in Section 354.9 of the Code of Iowa are hereby adopted in full. For
purposes herein, all land located within two miles distance from the City’s
boundaries shall be subject to the review provisions of the referenced Code of
Iowa chapter. The provisions of
Chapter 161 of this Code of Ordinances, Stormwater Detention Facilities, shall
be applicable to all land subject to the provisions of this chapter.
166.02   DEFINITIONS.
For the purpose of this chapter the following terms or words shall be
interpreted or defined as follows.
1.   “Acquisition plat” means the graphical representation of the division of
land or rights in land, created as the result of a conveyance or condemnation
for right-of-way purposes by an agency of the government or other persons
having the power of eminent domain.
2.   “Aliquot part” means a fractional part of a section within the United
States public land survey system. Only the fractional parts one-half, one-
quarter, one-half of one-quarter, or one-quarter of one-quarter are considered
an aliquot part of a section.
3.   “Alley” means a permanent service way providing a secondary means of
access to abutting lands.
4.   “Auditor’s plat” means a subdivision plat required by either the auditor
or the assessor, prepared by a surveyor under the direction of the Auditor.
5.   “Block” means property abutting on one side of a street, and lying between
the two nearest intersecting and intercepting streets, or between the nearest
intersecting and intercepting street or railroad right-of-way, waterway, or
other definite barrier.
6.   “Building setback line” means the line nearest the front of, and across, a
lot establishing the minimum open space to be provided between the front line
of buildings and structures and the street right-of-way lines.
7.   “Commission” is the City Planning and Zoning Commission.
8.   “Comprehensive Plan” is the complete plan, or any of its parts, for the
development of the City, prepared by the Commission and adopted in accordance
with Chapter 117, Acts of 1925, General Assembly of Iowa, and all acts
amendatory thereto, as now or may be in effect.
9.   “Condominium” means a building containing two or more dwelling units which
are designed and intended to be separately owned in fee.
10.   “Conveyance” means an instrument filed with a recorder as evidence of the
transfer of title to land, including any form of deed or contract.
11.   “Division” means dividing a tract or parcel of land into two parcels of
land by conveyance or for tax purposes. The conveyance of an easement, other
than a public highway easement, shall not be considered a division for the
purpose of this chapter.
12.   “Easement” means an authorization by a property owner for another to use
a designated part of said owner’s property for a specified purpose.
13.   “Flag lot” means a lot whose primary area for improvement purposes
consistent with zoning requirements does not directly abut a public street.
14.   “Lot” means a tract of land represented and identified by number or
letter designation on an official plat.
15.   “Metes and bounds description” means a description of land that uses
distances and angles, uses distances and bearings, or describes the boundaries
of the parcel by reference to physical features of the land.
16.   “Official plat” means either an auditor’s plat or subdivision plat that
meets the requirements of this chapter and has been filed for record in the
offices of the Recorder, Auditor, and Assessor.
17.   “Outlot” means a lot of record, within or without a subdivision, upon
which there is located no existing residential, commercial, industrial, or
mobile home improvement and/or upon which no specific use is enjoyed other than
a farm use as defined in Section
167.02(25) of this Code of Ordinances or as may otherwise be set forth herein,
and which lot is designated an “outlot” on any plat, survey or other depiction
thereof.
18.   “Parcel” means a part of a tract of land.
19.   “Plat” is a major chart indicating the subdivision or resubdivision of
land, intended to be filed for record.
20.   “Plat of survey” means the graphical representation of a survey of one or
more parcels of land, including a complete and accurate description of each
parcel within the plat, prepared by a registered land surveyor.
21.   “Resubdivision” means any subdivision of land that has previously been
included in a recorded plat. In appropriate context it may be a verb referring
to the act of preparing a plat of previously subdivided land.
22.   “Spot zoning” means rezoning of a lot or parcel of land to benefit an
owner for a use incompatible with surrounding uses and not for the purpose of
effect or furthering the Comprehensive Zoning Plan.
23.   “Street” means a right-of-way, dedicated to and accepted for the public
use, which affords the principal means of access to abutting property. A street
may be designated as a highway, thoroughfare, parkway, boulevard, road, avenue,
lane, drive, place, or other appropriate name. A street may also be identified
according to type of use, as described in the Thoroughfare Plan.
24.   “Subdivision,” for the purpose of these regulations, is either:
   A.   The division of land into two or more tracts, sites, or parcels.
   B.   The establishment or dedication of a road, highway, street, or avenue
through a tract of land regardless of area.
   C.   The resubdivision of land previously divided or platted into lots,
sites, or parcels, provided, however, that the sale or exchange of small
parcels of land to or between adjoining property owners, where such sale or
exchange does not create additional lots, is not considered a subdivision of
land.
   D.   The improvement of one or more parcels of land for residential,
commercial, or industrial structures or groups of structures involving the
division and/or allocation of land as for streets, utility easement for water,
sewer, storm sewer, electricity, telephone, etc., street access, open spaces,
and for common use, and other public facilities, as set out in this chapter, as
permitted in Chapters 354 and 355 of the Code of Iowa.
   E.   The improvement of any lot designated on a plat, survey, or other
depiction as an “outlot.” A subdivision shall not require the platting of
property where either of the following conditions exist: (i) no street
extension, new streets, road, alley, easement, open spaces, common ground, or
other public interest is being conveyed; or (ii) the plat is for assessment and
taxation purposes only. Where either of the conditions named herein exist, the
plat shall be submitted to the Council, which shall approve the plat by
resolution and affix a certified copy of the resolution for recording with the
plat.
25.   “Thoroughfare Plan” means the part of the Comprehensive Plan, now or
hereafter adopted which sets forth the location, alignment, dimensions,
identification, and classification of existing and proposed public streets,
highways, and other thoroughfares. The types of streets in the City’s
Thoroughfare Plan are: expressway, municipal arterial, municipal arterial
collector, municipal feeder, and residential street. (See Section
166.07)
   A.   “Expressway system streets” are those designated in the Thoroughfare
Plan. Expressway system streets are planned for high volumes of traffic
movement, either around the City or through the City.
   B.   “Municipal arterial streets” are those designated in the Thoroughfare
Plan for medium to large volumes of traffic movement. Certain arterial streets
may be classified as business streets to serve congested business sections, and
others may be classified as limited access highways to which entrances and
exits are provided only at controlled intersections, with access denied to
abutting properties.
   C.   “Municipal arterial collector streets” are those so designated in the
Thoroughfare Plan. These will consist of those streets within the City that
collect traffic from the municipal service system and connect to the major
arterial system.
   D.   “Municipal feeder streets” are designated in the Thoroughfare Plan as
important streets for the following reasons: (i) to facilitate collecting
residential traffic and (ii) to connect with the arterial system.
   E.   “Residential street system” are all those streets not designated in the
Thoroughfare Plan listed above.
   F.   “Industrial street or roadway” (concurrent classification). In addition
to the classifications set forth in the preceding section, the City may
concurrently designate a street as an industrial street or roadway, which
street or roadway shall be subject to additional or alternative improvement and
construction standards by virtue of actual or anticipated consistent and
frequent use by vehicles weighing in excess of 30,000 pounds. The Council shall
specifically designate a street as an industrial street or roadway and such
designation may be made at the time of the platting of property or at any time
prior to the installation of a street in a subdivision.
26.   “Tract” means an aliquot part of a section, a lot within an official
plat, or a government lot.
27.   “Zoning Administrator” means the person appointed by the Council to
administer and enforce this chapter and carry out other duties as outlined in
this Code of Ordinances.
166.03   PREPARATION OF PRELIMINARY PLAT.
1.   Whenever the owner of any tract or parcel of land within the corporate
limits of the City, or within two miles thereof, wishes to make a subdivision
of same, the owner shall submit 20 copies of said preliminary plat along with
other information described herein. The submission of these documents and
information shall be to the Zoning Administrator. Submission to the Zoning
Administrator shall be at least 13 working days prior to the scheduled
Commission meeting at which action upon the preliminary plat is desired. The
Zoning Administrator has the authority to review a preliminary plat and return
it to the applicant within three working days of its submission. If there are
no infractions or omissions, the Zoning Administrator shall distribute the same
to the appropriate City officers.
2.   The Zoning Administrator shall provide each applicant requesting a
residential preliminary plat approval with two notification signs containing
the date, time, and place of the Planning and Zoning Commission meeting. Said
signs shall be clearly posted by the applicant on the property for which the
request has been made. The signs must be placed so that they may be seen from a
street, and, on corner lots, a sign shall be posted on both frontages. The
applicant is responsible for seeing that signs are posted 10 days before the
Commission meeting and remain posted until the Commission meeting, after which
they must be removed and returned to City Hall within 72 hours after the
Commission meeting. If the notifications signs are not posted, the Commission
may not take action.
3.   Some (or all) of the preliminary plat requirements may be waived, upon
approval of the Zoning Administrator and City Engineer, on the subdivision of
two lots, provided that both lots within the proposed subdivision front an
existing, improved City street and no public improvements construction is
required.
166.04   APPLICATION FOR PRELIMINARY APPROVAL.
A person desiring preliminary approval of a plat of a subdivision shall submit
a written application to the Zoning Administrator. Such application shall be
accompanied by the following information and plans:
1.   Location Map. The location map need not be a special drawing. The
following data may be shown by notations on available City maps:
   A.   Subdivision name and location.
   B.   Major thoroughfares related to the subdivision.
   C.   Public transportation lines.
   D.   Main shopping center.
   E.   Community or neighborhood stores.
   F.   Elementary and high schools.
   G.   Parks and playgrounds.
   H.   Other community features.
   I.   Title, scale, north point and date.
2.   Site Map. A site map showing:
   A.   Topographical data in one of the following forms, which shall be
determined by the Commission during preliminary consideration of the plan:
      (1)   A contour map with contours at intervals of two feet if the general
slope of the site is less than 10 percent, and at vertical intervals of five
feet if the general slope is greater than 10 percent.
      (2)   A land inspection sketch showing terrain features, wooded areas,
buildings, and other natural or artificial features which would affect the plan
of the subdivision.
   B.   Tract boundary lines, showing dimensions, bearings, angles, and
references to section, township, and range lines or corners.
   C.   Streets and right-of-way, on or adjoining the site, including dedicated
widths, roadway widths, approximate gradients, types and width of pavements,
curbs, location of streetlights, sidewalks, tree planting, and other pertinent
data.
   D.   Locations, widths, and purposes of easements.
   E.   Utilities, including sanitary and storm sewers, other drainage
facilities, water lines, gas mains, electric utilities, and other facilities.
Size or capacity of each should be shown and the locations of distance to each
existing utility indicated.
   F.   Zoning of the site and adjoining property.
   G.   Other features or conditions which would affect the subdivision
favorably or adversely.
   H.   Title, scale, north point, and date.
3.   A preliminary plat of the subdivision, drawn to scale of 50 feet to one
inch or 60 feet to one inch, provided, however, that if the resulting drawing
would be over 36 inches in shortest dimension, two or more pages may be used.
The preliminary plat shall show:
   A.   Proposed name of the subdivision.
   B.   Names and addresses of owner and subdivider, land planning consultant,
surveyor, or engineer, with seal and signature of the person who prepared the
plan.
   C.   Street pattern showing the names (which shall not duplicate names of
other streets in the community except in cases of extensions of existing
streets) and widths of right-of-way of streets, sidewalks, easements, or
alleys.
   D.   Layout of lots, showing dimensions and numbers, square foot area of
each lot with irregular sides (not rectangular), block number (if required),
distances, radii, and chords.
   E.   Parcels of land proposed to be dedicated or reserved for schools,
parks, playgrounds, or other public, semi-public, or community purposes.
   F.   Building setback line.
   G.   Key plan, legend, and notes.
   H.   Scale, north point, and date.
4.   Engineering plans showing:
   A.   Profiles, typical cross-sections, and specifications for proposed
street improvements.
   B.   Profiles and locations and other explanatory data concerning the
installation of sanitary sewer and storm systems and water distribution system.
5.   A description of the protective covenants or private restrictions to be
incorporated in the plat of the subdivision.
6.   Information as to any agreements which have been entered into with the
owners of other property within the neighborhood in which the proposed
subdivision is located, as to general plans for the entire neighborhood.
Reference would be made to the Comprehensive Plan for suggestions as to the
general street pattern and design of the neighborhood. Whenever possible all of
the property owners within the neighborhood should endeavor to agree upon a
general plan for its development, in order that each subdivision may be
designed as an integral part of a well-considered overall plan.
7.   The application shall be accompanied by a certified check or money order
payable to the City, in the amount of $100.00, plus $5.00 for each lot, to
cover the cost of checking and verifying the proposed plat, and this amount
shall be deposited in the General Fund of the City.
166.05   PRELIMINARY PLAT APPROVAL.
1.   Upon the filing of 20 copies of the preliminary plat, which should include
11 copies of 50 feet to one inch scale, eight copies of 11 inches by 17 inches,
and one electronic copy, the Zoning Administrator has the authority to review a
preliminary plat and return it to the applicant within three working days of
its submission. If there are no infractions or omissions, the Zoning
Administrator shall distribute the copies of the plat as follows: one copy to
the City Engineer; one copy to the City Attorney; one copy to the Director of
Public Works; one copy to each member of the Commission; and where a proposed
plat is outside the City limits but within the area of subdivision
jurisdiction, one copy to the Zoning Administrator of the County. One copy
shall be retained by the Zoning Administrator. The City Engineer, Zoning
Administrator, Director of Public Works, and where concerned, the Zoning
Administrator for the County, shall have opportunity to review the plat and
application materials to assure the proposed subdivision complies with
applicable regulations and requirements and report upon such to the Commission.
The Zoning Administrator shall determine if the proposed subdivision complies
with the Zoning regulations. The Zoning Administrator shall also report upon
conditions of the site or adjacent properties, which, while not evident in the
application materials, may affect development upon the site.
2.   After an application for approval of a plat of a subdivision has been
filed with the Zoning Administrator at least 13 working days prior to the time
of the next regularly scheduled meeting of the Commission, the Commission shall
review the application and shall study such preliminary plat. The Commission
shall see if the plat conforms to the minimum standards and requirements as
outlined in this chapter, and shall recommend approval or rejection of such
plat within 30 days after submission. Upon approval of the plat by the
Commission, the Zoning Administrator shall notify the Clerk of the same, at
which time the Clerk shall place discussion of the plat on the agenda for the
next scheduled meeting of the Council.
3.   If the Commission does not act within 30 days, the preliminary plat shall
be deemed to be approved; unless the subdivider would agree to an extension of
the time, for a period not to exceed 60 days. The Commission shall submit its
recommendations to the Council for its action by resolution. The approval of
the preliminary plat by the Council does not constitute approval of the
subdivision, but is merely an authorization to proceed with the preparation of
the final plat.
4.   One copy of the preliminary plat approved by the Council and signed by the
Mayor and City Clerk, and shall be maintained in the office of the Zoning
Administrator. One copy is authorization for the subdivider to proceed with the
preparation of the final plat.
166.06   DURATION OF APPROVAL OF PRELIMINARY PLAT.
An approval of the preliminary plat shall be effective for a period of 18
months, unless, upon request of the applicant, the Council grants an extension.
The final plat shall be submitted to the Zoning Administrator and if it is not
received within the period of time specified above, all previous actions by the
Council with respect to the plat shall be deemed to be null and void.
166.07   DESIGN PRINCIPLES AND STANDARDS.
The preliminary plat of the subdivision shall conform to the following
principles and standards of design.
1.   General. The subdivision plat shall conform to the principles and
standards, which are generally exhibited in the Comprehensive Plan.
2.   Streets.
   A.   Proposed streets should be adjusted to the contour of the land so as to
produce usable lots and streets of reasonable gradient.
   B.   The street and alley layout shall conform to the Thoroughfare Plan for
the development of the neighborhood in which the proposed subdivision is
located and shall provide access to all lots and parcels of land within the
subdivision. Where streets cross other streets, jogs shall not be created. The
minimum distance between centerlines of parallel or approximately parallel
streets intersecting a cross street should be 300 feet.
   C.   Certain proposed streets where appropriate, shall be extended to the
boundary line of the tract to be subdivided so as to provide for normal
circulation of traffic within the vicinity.
   D.   Whenever there exists a dedicated or platted portion of a street or
alley adjacent to the proposed subdivision, the remainder of the street or
alley to the prescribed width shall be platted within the proposed subdivision.
Proposed utilities shall be extended to the boundary line of the tract to be
subdivided so as to provide for future development.
   E.   The width and right-of-way of streets shall conform to the width
specifications according to the following categories:
Thoroughfare Plan
Type of Street Minimum      Minimum
               Right-of-way Paving Width
Type of Street                                    Minimum      Minimum
                                                  Right-of-way Paving Width
Expressway System Street
(Defined as expressway system streets planned for 150 feet     12 feet per lane
high volume of traffic movement, either around
the City or through the City)
Municipal Arterial Street
(Defined to include State and County roads and
highway as well as City streets, which serve as   80 feet      44 feet
major thoroughfares to carry into and through the
City)
Municipal Arterial Collector Streets
(Defined as a street serving as a connection or
feeder from local streets to major streets,       60 feet      38 feet *
serving as direct access route to the various
subdivisions, and business areas of the City, or
access entering or leaving the City)
Municipal Feeder Street
(Defined as street aiding the collector system to 60 feet      33 feet *
facilitate the collection of traffic from the
subdivision and business areas)
