streets by resolution of the Council.
 
   F.   Notwithstanding the above categorization, culs-de-sac shall terminate
in a circular right-of-way having a minimum diameter of 100 feet, with a
minimum paving radius of 40 feet, culs-de-sac in business and industrial
districts shall have a minimum paving radius of 60 feet. The length of culs-de-
sac shall not exceed 600 feet (these requirements may be modified by the City
upon the recommendation of the City Engineer and the City Public Works
Director, in light of the nature and volume of traffic projected to use the
culs-de-sac street). Specific streets shall be classified in accordance with
the above by a resolution of the Council or as may be shown on a Thoroughfare
Plan of the City.
   G.   If the subdivider plats a subdivision as defined in this Code and makes
use of an existing concrete industrial roadway or street, said subdivider shall
be required to add one additional minimum 12-foot wide lane of concrete (in
accordance with Public Works requirements) to the existing industrial street or
roadway and shall further be required to add the appropriate shoulder. If such
subdivider makes use of an existing street which is not improved with concrete,
that subdivider shall install one-half of the street. In either case,
construction shall be in accordance with paving and construction standards
established elsewhere in this Code with the approval of the City Engineer and
the Public Works Director.
      (1)   Alleys shall be at least 20 feet in width.
      (2)   The centerlines of streets should intersect as nearly at right
angles as possible.
      (3)   Where an alley intersects a street property line, corners shall be
rounded by arcs of at least 20 feet radii or by chords of such arcs.
      (4)   At intersections of streets, the property line corners shall be
rounded by arcs with radii of not less than 15 feet, or by chords of such arcs.
      (5)   If the smaller angle of the intersection of two streets is less
than 60 degrees, the radius of the intersection of property lines shall be
increased as deemed advisable by the Commission.
      (6)   Intersections of more than two streets at one point shall be
avoided.
      (7)   Whenever the proposed subdivision contains or is adjacent to a
highway designated as a limited access highway by the appropriate highway
authorities, provision shall be made for a marginal access street or a parallel
street at a distance acceptable for the appropriate use of the land between the
highway and such street.
      (8)   Unobstructed sight distances measured from a point five feet above
the proposed grade line, to permit horizontal visibility on all streets, must
be established along the centerline of such streets as follows:
         a.   Limited access highways: to be determined by the Commission, but
generally not less than 500 feet.
         b.   Arterial streets and parkways: 600 feet.
         c.   Feeder and residential streets: 300 feet.
      (9)   Curvature measured along the centerline shall have a minimum radius
as follows:
         a.   Limited access highways: 1,000 feet.
         b.   Arterial streets: 500 feet.
         c.   Parkways: 300 feet.
         d.   Feeder and residential streets: 200 feet.
      (10)   Between reversed curves on arterial streets, a tangent of not less
than 200 feet shall be provided, and on feeder and residential streets, such a
tangent shall be not less than 100 feet.
      (11)   Maximum or minimum grades.
         a.   Arterial streets, not greater than 4 percent.
         b.   Feeder and residential streets, not greater than 6 percent.
         c.   The minimum grade of any street gutter shall not be less than 0.3
percent.
3.   Blocks.
   A.   Blocks shall not exceed 800 feet in length in residential zoning
districts.
   B.   Blocks for commercial or industrial zoned districts shall be reviewed
by the Commission.
   C.   Blocks shall be of sufficient width to permit two tiers of lots of
appropriate depth except where an interior street parallels a limited access
highway or arterial street.
4.   Lots.
   A.   All lots shall abut on a street.
   B.   Side lines of lots shall be at approximately right angles to straight
streets and on radial lines on curved streets. Some variation from this rule is
permissible, but pointed or very irregular lots shall be avoided.
   C.   Double frontage lots shall not be platted, except that where desired
along arterial streets or limited access highways, lots may face on an interior
street and back on such thoroughfares. In that event, a strip at least 20 feet
in width shall be provided along the back of the lot for plantings or
screening.
   D.   The depth-to-width ratio of the usable area of a lot shall be at a
maximum of 3.0 to 1.0.
   E.   Corner residential lots shall be wider than normal in order to permit
appropriate setbacks from both streets.
   F.   No property shall be platted as an outlot or otherwise designated as an
outlot on any plat, survey, or similar depiction, unless use of said outlot is
restricted to a farm use approved by
Chapter 167 of this Code of Ordinances, within a subdivision and the platting
of a parcel of ground as an outlot shall not be deemed to eliminate any
required subdivision improvements. No outlot may be improved or used other than
is set forth herein without further platting, nor shall any use of an outlot
involve the violation of zoning or building requirements, regarding side yards,
setback lines, or similar restrictions. No outlot shall be improved without
giving consideration to, and complying with, the Comprehensive Plan, proposed
street, easement layout, and similar restrictions established by the City.
   G.   Flag lots are not permitted in new subdivisions or resubdivisions of
existing platted subdivisions. Flag lots currently in existence may be improved
as long as the portion of said lot adjacent to an existing public street has a
minimum frontage of 40 feet and as long as all applicable zoning or subdivision
requirements are met.
5.   Easements.
   A.   Utility easements of not less than 10 feet shall be provided along rear
lot lines and alongside lot lines where needed. When the property does not
adjoin another subdivision, where an easement has been provided, then an
easement of not less than 20 feet shall be provided. Easements of greater width
may be required where needed. Easements shall be at final grade before any
utilities are provided for the property and the subdivider, contractor, or
builder shall keep all easements free of any excavation dirt, construction
material, or any other obstacles during construction.
   B.   Whenever any stream or important surface water course is located in an
area that is being subdivided, the subdivider shall, at his or her own expense,
make adequate provision for straightening or widening the channel so that it
will properly carry the surface water, and shall also provide and dedicate to
the City an easement along each side of the stream, which easement shall be for
the purpose of widening, improving, or protecting the stream and for
recreational use. The width of such easement shall not be less than 20 feet and
the total width of the easement shall be adequate to provide for any necessary
channel relocations and straightening.
6.   Building Setback Lines. Such lines shall be established back of highway
and street right-of-way lines as established by the Thoroughfare Plan, and in
no case shall the building setback lines be less than 25 feet.
7.   Public Open Space. Where sites for parks, schools, playgrounds, or other
public uses are located within the subdivision area as shown on the
Comprehensive Plan, or where such sites appear to be desirable, the Commission
may request their dedication for such purposes, or their reservation for a
period of one year following the date of the approval of the plat. In the event
a governmental agency concerned passes a resolution expressing its intent to
acquire the land so reserved, the reservation period shall be extended for an
additional six months.
Where the subdivider can show that the strict application of the requirements
contained in this section would cause unnecessary hardship because of
topographical or other conditions peculiar to the site, the Council, upon
recommendation of the Commission, may vary or modify such requirements so that
the subdivider is allowed to develop the property in a reasonable manner; but
so, at the same time, the public welfare and interest of the City and
surrounding area are protected and the general intent and spirit of these
regulations are preserved.
166.08   PRELIMINARY PLAT APPROVAL NOT TO CONSTITUTE SUBDIVISION APPROVAL.
Approval of the preliminary plat by the Council does not constitute approval of
the subdivision, but is merely an authorization to the subdivider to proceed
with the preparation of the final plat.
166.09   FINAL PLAT REQUIREMENTS.
The final plat shall meet the following specifications:
1.   The final plat may include all or any part of the approved preliminary
plat.
2.   The original drawing of the final plat of the subdivision shall be drawn
to a scale of 50 feet to one inch, or 60 feet to one inch, provided, however,
that if the resulting drawing shall be over 36 inches in shortest dimension,
two or more pages may be used. 20 copies, which include 11 copies of 50 feet to
one inch scale, eight copies of 11 inches by 17 inches, and one electronic
copy, shall be submitted with the original final plat, or, in order to conform
to modern drafting and reproduction methods, lettering may be applied to the
final plat in a manner which will permit the plat to be reproduced by film,
litholoid, or other photographic process at the designated scale, and in such
case 10 black line prints, a reproducible print and 10 copies shall be
submitted. Submission of the final plat shall be to the Zoning Administrator at
least 13 working days prior to the next regular Commission meeting, and the
Zoning Administrator shall distribute said final plat (and other required
documents under this section) in the manner stated in Section
166.05(1).
3.   The following basic information shall be shown:
   A.   Accurate boundary lines, with dimensions and angles, which provide a
survey of the tract closing with an error of not more than one foot in 5,000
feet. Submission of the final plat shall be accompanied by submission of full
and complete construction plans and specifications regarding the construction
of streets, sidewalks, storm sewers, and drainage facilities.
   B.   Accurate distances and directions to the nearest established street
corners or official monuments. Reference corners shall be accurately described
on the plat.
   C.   Accurate locations of all existing and recorded streets intersecting
the boundaries of the tract.
   D.   Accurate metes and bounds description of the boundary.
   E.   Source of title to the land as shown by the books of the County
Recorder of the County in which the land is located.
   F.   Street names.
   G.   Complete curve notes for all curves included in the plat.
   H.   Street lines with accurate dimensions in feet and hundredths of feet,
with angles to street, alley, and lot lines.
   I.   Lot numbers and dimensions.
   J.   Easements for utilities including street lights and any limitations of
such easements.
   K.   Accurate dimensions for any property to be dedicated or reserved for
public, semi-public, or community use.
   L.   Building setback line and dimensions.
   M.   Location, type, material, and size of all monuments and lot markers.
   N.   Restrictions of all types which will run with the land and become
covenants in the deeds for lots.
   O.   Name of the subdivision.
   P.   Name and address of the owner and subdivider.
   Q.   North point, scale, and date.
   R.   Certification by a registered professional engineer or registered land
surveyor.
   S.   Certificate of dedication of streets and other public property.
   T.   The final plat shall contain a statement that all improvements to the
subdivision will be completed to the specifications of the City.
4.   When the final plat is submitted to the Council, it shall be accompanied
by the following instruments, and each of these instruments must be submitted
to the City Attorney for approval. This approval must be obtained in writing
prior to submission of the documents to the Council. It is the subdivider’s
responsibility to secure such approval.
   A.   A statement by the proprietors and their spouses, if any, that the plat
is prepared with their free consent and in accordance with their desire, signed
and acknowledged before an officer authorized to take the acknowledgments of
deeds. The statement by the proprietors may also include a dedication to the
public of all lands within the plat that are designated for streets, alleys,
parks, open areas, school property, or other public use, if the dedication is
approved by the Council.
   B.   An opinion by an attorney-at-law who has examined the abstract of title
of the land being platted. The opinion shall state the names of the proprietors
and holders of mortgages, liens, or other encumbrances on the land being
platted and shall note the encumbrances, along with any bonds securing the
encumbrances. Utility easements shall not be construed to be encumbrances for
the purpose of this section.
   C.   A certificate of the County Treasurer that the land is free from
certified taxes and certified special assessments or that the land is free from
certified taxes and that the certified special assessments are secured by bond
in compliance with Section 354.12 of the Code of Iowa.
   D.   A statement from the mortgage holders or lienholders, if any, that the
plat is prepared with their free consent and in accordance with their desire,
signed and acknowledged before an officer authorized to take the acknowledgment
of deeds. An affidavit and bond as provided for in Section 354.12 of the Code
of Iowa may be recorded in lieu of the consent of the mortgage or lienholder.
When a mortgage or lienholder consents to the subdivision, a release of
mortgage or lien shall be recorded for any areas conveyed to the City or
dedicated to the public.
   E.   A resolution and certificate for approval by the Council and for
signatures of the Mayor and Clerk.
   F.   Either a certificate that all improvements and installation shall be
completed, or a cash surety bond, both further described below:
      (1)   A certificate bearing the approval of the City Engineer stating
that all improvements and installations to the subdivision required by this
chapter shall be made or installed in accordance with the specifications of the
City, and a letter from the Public Works Director stating the same, and that
there is on file a four-year cash maintenance bond for all improvements,
approved by the City Engineer and City Attorney before acceptance, with the
provision that the aforesaid four-year cash maintenance bond shall be subject
to the numbered provision for arbitration set out in Paragraph (3) below. In
lieu of the submission of a cash surety (completion) bond, the subdivider may
submit an irrevocable letter of credit in compliance with the provisions of
this paragraph, subject to the approval of the Council, City Engineer and City
Attorney. In circumstances where a plat is located in an area where public
infrastructure does not presently exist or is in an area where improvements to
public infrastructure may be expanded or improved and in the opinion of the
Council, development does not warrant present installation of subdivision
improvements, the Council may require that a standard assessment waiver form
provided by the City be filed with the plat in lieu of an engineer’s
certificate or cash equivalent surety bond. The provisions of Paragraph (3)
below regarding arbitration proceedings shall not be applicable to the City’s
implementation of provisions of an assessment waiver or the special assessment
process.
      (2)   In the event that a surety or completion bond is necessary for
construction, there shall be submitted a cash surety bond with the City which
shall insure to the City that all improvements will be completed by the
subdivider or property owners within the two years after official acceptance of
the plat. The form, type, and disposition of the bond in the event of discharge
against same, shall be subject to the provisions of Paragraph (3) immediately
below, and the specific language, cash denomination, and the cash bond which
shall be in the form of cash time certificates or savings accounts at a local
bank, shall be approved in writing by the City Attorney, City Engineer, and
City Council, and the amount of the bond shall be not less than 115 percent of
the estimated cost of the improvement. If the improvements are not completed in
the specified time, the Council may use the bond or any necessary portion
thereof to complete the same, all at the discretion of the Council subject to
Paragraph (3) below. No building permits shall be issued on any portion of the
subdivision unless said portion has been approved and the improvements accepted
by the Council. A four-year cash maintenance bond shall be required for all
improvements, and the cash maintenance bond shall be approved as set out above,
by the City Attorney, City Engineer and the Council. A cash maintenance bond
submitted pursuant to the provisions of this paragraph shall be for a
percentage of the estimated improvement costs determined by the Council by
resolution. In lieu of the submission of a cash maintenance bond for
improvements, the subdivider may submit an irrevocable letter of credit (for
the prescribed amount) to be approved by the City Council, City Engineer, and
City Attorney. Additionally in lieu of a cash maintenance bond for
improvements, a subdivider may submit a maintenance bond from a bonding company
approved by the City, under such terms and conditions as meet the intent of
this paragraph. Notwithstanding the preceding, if a bonding company maintenance
bond is provided, the provisions of next Paragraph (3) shall not be applicable.
Notwithstanding the preceding, in lieu of a cash surety bond or irrevocable
letter of credit, a subdivider may submit a surety bond from a bonding company
approved by the City, under such terms and conditions as meet the intent of
this paragraph. If a bonding company surety bond is provided, the provisions of
the next Paragraph (3) shall not be applicable.
      (3)   The paragraphs set out above define surety and maintenance bonds,
and define the period for which said bonds shall be effective. It is
specifically provided with regard to these bonds however, that the Council may
and in many cases shall, require that the bonds in either event be in the form
of cash time certificates or interest bearing savings accounts in favor of the
bonded individual or development, but set up in so far as ownership in a manner
which allows the bank holding the time certificate or savings account to
disburse the proceeds of same directly upon the authority of the of the
Council, subject to the following:
         a.   In the event it becomes necessary, according to the discretion of
the Council, to exercise against the surety or maintenance bond provided for
herein, the Council shall at that time notify the subdivider or developer that
all or a portion of the bond may be attached for completion, maintenance, or
reconstruction of the indicated project, and that if the subdivider or
developer disputes the figures determined by the Council for the setoff against
such cash bond, then he or she may elect, by notice in writing to the Council,
delivered within 30 days of the date that notice of intent to exercise against
the bond has been mailed by ordinary mail at the address defined in the escrow
bond agreement with the City and escrow bank, to effect arbitration procedures
as defined herein. In that event, the developer shall choose an individual for
arbitration of any dispute regarding the amount and necessity of cash setoff
against the maintenance or surety bond, and the Council shall likewise select
an arbitrator who may be, but need not be an Attorney at Law, and the two
arbitrators shall select a third arbitrator. It shall be the duty of the three
arbitrators to determine within 60 days of the date of their commission, what,
if any, setoffs are necessary against the cash bond to effect the proper
maintenance, repair, completion, construction, or reconstruction necessitated
by the alleged default against the cash bond, and to make its recommendation in
writing to the Council and the developer or subdivider. The Council shall then
proceed to certify the recommendation and agreement of the arbitration board
and shall notify the Bank Escrow Agent to release that indicated amount to the
City pursuant to the authority defined above and further set out in the bank
escrow agreement.
         b.   In the event the developer does not choose to dispute the cash
setoff defined by the Council as necessary to complete, construct, reconstruct,
maintain, or repair the indicated project, which is the subject of the bond
controversy, then the initial defined amount of the Council shall be that
amount certified by the Council to the Bank Escrow Agent and paid by the Bank
Escrow Agent in favor of the City.
         c.   In the event the developer or subdivider does not serve notice in
writing to the Council of his or her intent to elect arbitration within the
defined timetable above, such person shall be presumed to have acquiesced in
the setoff demands of the Council, and certification by the Council at that
time to the Bank Escrow Agent shall similarly call for payment by the escrow
agent in favor of the City.
         d.   The method of determining arbitration individuals shall be at the
discretion of the parties indicated above, subject however to the following:
The subdivider or developer shall first choose and determine an arbitrator,
within 30 days of the date that he or she serves notice upon the City of the
intent to elect an arbitration of the dispute. The Council shall have 30 days
from the date they receive written notice of the selection of the subdivider/
developer’s arbitrator, to select their own arbitration individual, after which
the two arbitrators so selected shall have an additional 30 day period to agree
upon a satisfactory third arbitration individual. If the developer fails to
comply with the defined timetable in selecting an arbitrator, he or she shall
again be presumed to acquiesce to the initial demands of the Council with
regard to the cash setoff initially demanded against the bond, and in that
event, upon certification by the Council, the Bank Escrow Agent shall pay out
the indicated sum in favor of the City. In the event that the two arbitrators
selected by the developer and the Council cannot agree upon a satisfactory
third arbitrator, within the defined timetable, or in the event that the three
arbitrators, once selected, cannot come to an agreement with regard to a
specific sum and/or other specific remedy as the situation, by maintenance,
construction, or reconstruction by the original developer, then the arbitrators
shall be discharged of their commission to negotiate and determine the dispute,
and another arbitration board shall be reestablished according to the same
timetable and definition as set out above for the first. This procedure shall
continue until either the developer acquiesces in the initial setoff demands of
the Council, or an arbitration board is selected which reaches a final
consensus agreement as to defined dollar setoff against the arbitration demand
or defines other satisfactory redress in favor of the City to alleviate the
cause of the bond setoff demand. The costs of arbitration shall be borne by the
subdivider or developer, to the extent of the initial arbitrator chosen by said
subdivider or developer for his or her benefit, or any successor arbitrators
chosen in methods defined above or necessitated by the result of health,
disability, or death intervention, and it shall similarly be the obligation of
the subdivider/developer to pay one-half the cost and reasonable compensation
required by the third arbitrator selected by the two previously named
arbitrators. The City shall pay the costs and compensation of the arbitrator
chosen by the City, and one-half of the costs of the third arbitrator selected
above. These methods of arbitration shall be final binding upon any subdivider
or developer who acknowledges a specific bond maintenance agreement or bond
escrow agreement in favor that the City pursuant to the definition above, and
no appeal from the final judgment of the arbitrators or disposition by the
Council as defined above shall lie.
   G.   State approved plans and profiles of all sanitary sewers, water mains,
and appurtenances.
   H.   A letter from the subdivider’s engineer stating the quantities of
excavation, streets, sewers, water mains, and other necessary improvements, if
a cash surety bond is to be filed, with the approval of the City Engineer.
   I.   A “hold harmless” agreement protecting the City from any damages,
claims, or suits resulting from the construction and development by the owner
and/or subdivider. Said agreement shall be approved as to format by the City
Attorney, and recorded with the plat.
166.10   FINAL PLAT APPROVAL.
1.   Upon the receipt of the final plat by the Zoning Administrator, it shall
be referred to the Planning and Zoning Commission for its review and
recommendations thereon to the Council. Upon the Commission’s action, said
action shall be forwarded to the Clerk who shall place discussion of the final
plat on the agenda for the next scheduled meeting of the Council.
2.   If the Commission does not approve the final plat of the subdivision, the
Council may approve said plat only by a three-fourths vote of the entire
membership of the Council.
3.   Council approval of the final plat shall be by resolution. The Council
shall direct the Mayor and City Clerk to certify the resolution and affix same
to the final plat.
4.   The final plat shall be filed by the applicant with the County Recorder
within four months of date of approval by the Council, and if not filed within
such time shall have no validity and shall not be recorded without re-
certification by the Clerk and re-approval by the Council. Before it is
recorded in the office of the County Recorder, the provisions of Chapter 354
and 355 of the Code of Iowa, shall be complied with. Immediately after
recording, three certified copies and one original size copy of the final plat
shall be filed with the Zoning Administrator.
166.11   RESOLUTIONS AND CERTIFICATES.
The following forms (or substantially similar forms) shall be used in
certifying the approval of the final plats.

We the undersigned ____________________________________, owners of the real

keep trimmed any trees or shrubs that interfere or threaten to interfere with

“Easement,” but same may be used for gardens, shrubs, landscaping and other
purposes that do not then or later interfere with the aforesaid uses or the
rights herein granted.
(Additional dedications and protective covenants, or private restrictions,
would be inserted here upon the subdivider’s initiative or the recommendation
of the Commission; important provisions are those specifying the use to be made
of the property and in the case of residential use, the minimum habitable floor
area.)
The foregoing covenants,(or restrictions), are to run with the land and shall
be binding on all parties and all persons claiming under them until January 1,
20____, (a 20-year period is suggested), at which time said covenants, (or
restrictions), shall be automatically extended for successive periods of 10
years unless changed by vote of a majority of the then owners of the building
sites covered by these covenants, or restrictions, which shall remain in full
force and effect.
The right to enforce these provisions by injunction, together with the right to
cause the removal, by due process of law, of any structure or part thereof
erected or maintained in violation hereof is dedicated to the public, and
reserved to the several owners of the several lots in this subdivision and to
their heirs and assigns.

166.12   PROHIBITION OF CONFLICTS OF INTEREST.
The City Engineer and City Attorney shall not be the engineer or attorney for
any improvements or subdivision within the City, other than municipal projects,
unless directly authorized by a three-fourths vote of the City Council.
166.13   ACCEPTANCE OF IMPROVEMENTS.
No improvements in any subdivision that has been approved by the Council shall
be officially accepted by the Council for the improvement and maintenance
thereof until the minimum improvements described in this chapter have been made
either by the subdivider or by the abutting property owners. In lieu of final
installments before the improvements are officially accepted, the subdivider or
property owners may follow the method set forth in this chapter. In all cases,
a four-year maintenance bond shall be required on all improvements.
166.14   IMPROVEMENT STANDARDS.
The final plat of the subdivision shall conform to the following standards of
improvements.
1.   Monuments and Markers.
   A.   Monuments and markers shall be placed so that the scored or marked
point shall coincide exactly with the intersection of lines to be marked, and
shall be set so that the top of the monument is level with the surface of the
surrounding ground.
   B.   Monuments shall be set at the intersection of all lines forming angles
in the boundary of the subdivision and at the corners of blocks where street
right-of-way lines intersect.
   C.   Markers shall be set at the beginning and ending of all curves along
street property lines, at all points where lot lines intersect curves along
street property lines, at all angles in property lines of lots, and at all
other lot corners not established by a monument.
   D.   Monuments shall be of concrete or stone with a minimum diameter of six
inches and a length of three feet, and shall be marked on top either with a
copper dowel set flush with the top of the monument or a cross scored deeply on
top. Markers shall consist of iron pipes, iron or steel bars at least three
feet long, and not less than five-eighths inch in diameter.
2.   Streets. All streets shall be filled or excavated to the grade approved by
the City Engineer and Public Works Director, and the roadway shall be improved
by surfacing. The minimum standards for surfacing shall be those described in
the Statewide Urban Design and Specifications (SUDAS), but may be modified upon
recommendation by the City Engineer and approval by the Public Works Director
and City Council. (The minimum width of surfacing shall be as set out in
Section
166.07.) Such surfacing shall be of a type conforming to the traffic
requirements of each street.
3.   Sewers.
   A.   The subdivider shall provide the subdivision with a complete sanitary
sewer system designed in compliance with the Statewide Urban Design and
Specifications (SUDAS), which shall connect with a sanitary sewer outlet
approved by the City Engineer, Public Works Director, and Council, except that
when such approved outlet is not available one of the following methods of
sewage disposal shall be used:
      (1)   A complete sanitary sewer system to convey the sewage to a
treatment plant, to be provided by the subdivider in accordance with minimum
requirements of the Statewide Urban Design and Specifications (SUDAS). Approval
shall be given by the Public Works Director, City Engineer, and Council.
      (2)   Private sewage disposal system on individual lots consisting of a
septic tank and tile absorption field or other approved sewage disposal system,
when laid out in accordance with the Statewide Urban Design and Specifications
(SUDAS) and approval by the City Engineer, Public Works Director, and the
Council, under the advisement of the County Health Department.
   B.   The plans for the installation of a sanitary sewer system shall be
prepared by the subdivider and approved by the City Engineer, Public Works
Director, and Council in compliance with the Statewide Urban Design and
Specifications (SUDAS). Upon the completion of the sanitary sewer installation,
the plans for such system “as built” shall be filed with the Public Works
Department or City Clerk. These “as built” plans shall comply with Statewide
Urban Design and Specifications (SUDAS) and shall show, at a minimum, the
following location: the footage from each side lot line, designated by a four-
inch by four-inch marker five feet long two feet above the grade and the
footage from the rear property line, as required.
   C.   In this subsection (“Sewers”) and the next subsection (“Water”) the
phrase “the subdivider shall provide” shall be interpreted to mean that the
subdivider shall install the facility referred to, or, whenever a private
sewage disposal system, or an individual water supply is to be provided, that
the subdivider shall require, as a condition of the sale of each lot or parcel
in the subdivision that the facilities referred to in these subsections shall
be installed by the developer of the lots in accordance with these regulations.
4.   Water.
   A.   The subdivider shall provide the subdivision with a complete water main
supply system, designed in compliance with the Statewide Urban Design and
Specifications (SUDAS), which shall be connected to a municipal or community
water supply approved by the Public Works Director, City Engineer and Council;
except, that when such municipal or community water supply is not available,
the subdivider shall provide on each lot in the subdivision in accordance with
minimum requirements of the City.
   B.   The plans for the installation of a water main supply system shall be
prepared by the subdivider and approved by the City Engineer, Public Works
Director, and Council. Upon the completion of the water supply installation,
the plans for such system “as built” shall be filed with the Public Works
Department or Clerk. These “as built” plans shall comply with City
specifications and shall show, at a minimum, the following: water mains,
valves, tees, laterals, corporations, curb stops, and all other accessories.
5.   Storm Drainage. The subdivider shall provide the subdivision with an
adequate underground storm sewer system throughout the entire subdivision,
which shall be separate and independent of the sanitary sewer system and which
shall provide an adequate outlet to other facilities. The system shall be
designed to adequately serve the area being platted for a 10-year design storm.
The system shall be constructed to provide connections for the pumped discharge
of water from drainage systems around and under foundations and basement floors
for each lot being developed in the subdivision. Construction must meet or
exceed the Statewide Urban Design and Specifications (SUDAS). Storm sewers
shall, be placed in either parkway between the curb and water main or sanitary
sewer main, or in an easement at rear lot lines. Storm drainage easements shall
be provided where necessary. The plans for installation of a storm drainage
system shall be prepared by the subdivider and approved by the City Engineer.
Upon the completion of said storm sewer system, the plans for same, “as built”
shall be filed with the Public Works Director.
6.   Curb and Gutter. Curbs and gutters shall be installed in all subdivisions
subject to the provisions of this chapter. The curbs and gutters shall be of
Portland cement concrete and shall be designed and installed in accordance with
the appropriate provisions of this Code of Ordinances.
7.   Sidewalks. Sidewalks shall be installed in all subdivisions subject to the
provisions of
Chapter 136. Such sidewalks shall be designed and installed in accordance with
the appropriate provisions of this Code of Ordinances.
166.15   IMPROVEMENT CREDIT PROCEDURE.
Improvements required in this chapter to be installed by the subdivider, which
are of a public utility nature, may provide benefits to properties other than
the subdivided property and which other properties are located in the vicinity
of the subdivided property. Upon the installation of subdivision improvements
which cross or adjoin other properties and can be used by such other
properties, the Council may, upon the connection to or use of the installation
by parties other than subdivider, within a period of 10 years following the
installation of the improvements, establish a reasonable connection fee
designed to compensate the subdivider for an appropriate share of said
improvements, which fee shall be credited to and paid to the subdivider.
1.   Construction Costs. The subdivider shall provide the City with
documentation of the estimated cost of the improvements as well as the actual
cost of said improvements.
2.   Basis for Recovery. Connection charges for water mains shall be based upon
a “front foot served” basis. Connection charges for storm and sanitary sewer
shall be on an “area served” basis with the area of influence clearly defined.
3.   Period of Payment. For a period of up to 10 years following the acceptance
of the improvements, such portion of the connection fees charged to adjacent or
other property owners as shall be determined by the Council to be appropriate,
shall be paid to the subdividers who installed and paid for the original
improvements, their heirs or assigns, unless a different amount is agreed upon
between the City and the subdivider.
4.   Enactment of Project. The specific terms for any project for which the
Council elects to subject to the terms of this amendment, shall be established
by Council resolution. Such resolution shall have the force and effect as if a
contract had been executed between the subdivider and the City.
5.   Standards. All installations pursuant to this chapter shall be to the
standards and specifications of the City.
6.   City as Subdivider. The term “subdivider” when used herein shall include,
when appropriate, the City (i.e. when the City installs such improvements as
are referenced herein).
7.   Plat and Legal Description Required. If the provisions of this section are
to be effective, the subdivider shall file with the Clerk and with the County
Recorder, a plat which shall show the following:
   A.   The subdivision in which the main improvements are to be installed.
   B.   All adjacent property in which improvements or extensions thereof have
been or are to be installed.
   C.   All adjacent property, which may be benefited by the installation of
the subdivision improvements or extensions thereof.
   D.   Said plat shall show the location of all improvements in benefited
areas and shall indicate such lengths, dimensions, etc. as shall enable a party
both to determine the location of the said improvements and to determine the
basis for recovery set forth in Subsection 2 above.
   E.   Accompanying said plat shall be an affidavit of the subdivider that the
plat contains a true and correct showing of the location and dimensions of the
improvements and extensions thereof, and that said plat is being submitted
pursuant to this section for the purpose of implementing subdivision
improvement credit procedures.
166.16   INSPECTION OF IMPROVEMENTS.
Fifty percent of the actual cost of engineering review fees related to planning
documents shall be charged to the subdivider.
166.17   ENFORCEMENT.
1.   No plat of any subdivision shall be entitled to be recorded in the County
Recorder’s Office, or have any validity until it shall have been approved in
the manner prescribed herein.
2.   The City shall not issue building or repair permits for any structure
located on a lot in any subdivision within the City, the plat of which has been
prepared after the adoption of this chapter but which has not been approved in
accordance with the provisions contained herein.
3.   The Council shall not permit public improvements over which it has no
control to be made, or any money expended for improvements in any area that has
been subdivided, or upon any street that has been platted after the date of an
adoption of this chapter, unless such subdivision or street has been approved
in accordance with the provisions contained herein.
166.18   VIOLATIONS; LIEN PROVISION.
A violation of any provision of this chapter shall be any one consecutive 24-
hour period during which a violation exists, and for each consecutive or non-
consecutive defined date an additional violation if the alleged violation is
not corrected. Each lot, parcel of land, or property affected by this
subdivision chapter shall be subject to lien certification in the event of such
violation, and said violation shall cause the City to file a notice of lien
against any said property, and said lien shall be enforced and effected as a
valid lien upon the real estate involved until purged by payment. In the event
that any person feels that he or she has not violated the provisions of this
chapter and should not be subject to the discretionary fine violation as set
above in lien procedures, such person may elect to have the dispute settled
pursuant to the arbitration provisions defined in this chapter. Any final
determination made by the arbitrators shall be certified by the City to a bond
escrow agent, and shall be paid by said bond escrow agent in favor of the City,
or, if no such bond in fact exists in the individual situation involved, then
lien procedures will be implemented against real estate owned or subdivided by
the developer, by certification of a lien to the County in which the real
estate is situated; and/or the lien shall be entered of record as a lis pendens
lien against the indicated developer or subdivider.
166.19   CHANGES AND AMENDMENTS.
Any regulations or provisions of this chapter may be changed and amended from
time to time by the City Council. However, such changes or amendments shall not
become effective until after study and report by the Planning and Zoning
Commission and until after a public hearing has been held, public notice of
which shall have been given in a newspaper of general circulation not less than
seven or more than 20 days before the date of said hearing.
